2025-01-24T13:52:24.2761079Z     @set_module('numpy')
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2761517Z     def load(file, mmap_mode=None, allow_pickle=False, fix_imports=True,
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2762282Z              encoding='ASCII', *, max_header_size=format._MAX_HEADER_SIZE):
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2762719Z         """
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2763109Z         Load arrays or pickled objects from ``.npy``, ``.npz`` or pickled files.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2763575Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2763971Z         .. warning:: Loading files that contain object arrays uses the ``pickle``
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2764645Z                      module, which is not secure against erroneous or maliciously
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2765213Z                      constructed data. Consider passing ``allow_pickle=False`` to
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2765773Z                      load data that is known not to contain object arrays for the
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2766244Z                      safer handling of untrusted sources.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2766600Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2766813Z         Parameters
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2767073Z         ----------
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2767388Z         file : file-like object, string, or pathlib.Path
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2767844Z             The file to read. File-like objects must support the
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2768314Z             ``seek()`` and ``read()`` methods and must always
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2768774Z             be opened in binary mode.  Pickled files require that the
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2769290Z             file-like object support the ``readline()`` method as well.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2769786Z         mmap_mode : {None, 'r+', 'r', 'w+', 'c'}, optional
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2770288Z             If not None, then memory-map the file, using the given mode (see
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2770840Z             `numpy.memmap` for a detailed description of the modes).  A
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2771417Z             memory-mapped array is kept on disk. However, it can be accessed
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2772185Z             and sliced like any ndarray.  Memory mapping is especially useful
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2772771Z             for accessing small fragments of large files without reading the
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2773248Z             entire file into memory.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2773619Z         allow_pickle : bool, optional
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2774098Z             Allow loading pickled object arrays stored in npy files. Reasons for
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2774750Z             disallowing pickles include security, as loading pickled data can
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2775374Z             execute arbitrary code. If pickles are disallowed, loading object
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2776075Z             arrays will fail. Default: False
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2776392Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2776634Z             .. versionchanged:: 1.16.3
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2777044Z                 Made default False in response to CVE-2019-6446.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2777426Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2777657Z         fix_imports : bool, optional
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2778133Z             Only useful when loading Python 2 generated pickled files on Python 3,
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2778774Z             which includes npy/npz files containing object arrays. If `fix_imports`
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2779390Z             is True, pickle will try to map the old Python 2 names to the new names
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2780053Z             used in Python 3.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2780378Z         encoding : str, optional
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2780835Z             What encoding to use when reading Python 2 strings. Only useful when
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2781444Z             loading Python 2 generated pickled files in Python 3, which includes
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2782281Z             npy/npz files containing object arrays. Values other than 'latin1',
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2782890Z             'ASCII', and 'bytes' are not allowed, as they can corrupt numerical
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2783377Z             data. Default: 'ASCII'
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2783727Z         max_header_size : int, optional
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2784211Z             Maximum allowed size of the header.  Large headers may not be safe
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2784829Z             to load securely and thus require explicitly passing a larger value.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2785379Z             See :py:func:`ast.literal_eval()` for details.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2785918Z             This option is ignored when `allow_pickle` is passed.  In that case
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2786521Z             the file is by definition trusted and the limit is unnecessary.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2786961Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2787180Z         Returns
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2787426Z         -------
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2787695Z         result : array, tuple, dict, etc.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2788171Z             Data stored in the file. For ``.npz`` files, the returned instance
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2788774Z             of NpzFile class must be closed to avoid leaking file descriptors.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2789234Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2789458Z         Raises
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2789702Z         ------
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2789935Z         OSError
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2790259Z             If the input file does not exist or cannot be read.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2790664Z         UnpicklingError
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2791063Z             If ``allow_pickle=True``, but the file cannot be loaded as a pickle.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2791534Z         ValueError
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2792120Z             The file contains an object array, but ``allow_pickle=False`` given.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2792596Z         EOFError
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2792993Z             When calling ``np.load`` multiple times on the same file handle,
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2793485Z             if all data has already been read
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2793837Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2794052Z         See Also
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2794303Z         --------
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2794583Z         save, savez, savez_compressed, loadtxt
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2795067Z         memmap : Create a memory-map to an array stored in a file on disk.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2795690Z         lib.format.open_memmap : Create or load a memory-mapped ``.npy`` file.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2796163Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2796365Z         Notes
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2796597Z         -----
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2796943Z         - If the file contains pickle data, then whatever object is stored
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2797434Z           in the pickle is returned.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2797883Z         - If the file is a ``.npy`` file, then a single array is returned.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2798414Z         - If the file is a ``.npz`` file, then a dictionary-like object is
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2798973Z           returned, containing ``{filename: array}`` key-value pairs, one for
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2799673Z           each file in the archive.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2800128Z         - If the file is a ``.npz`` file, the returned value supports the
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2800706Z           context manager protocol in a similar fashion to the open function::
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2801162Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2801386Z             with load('foo.npz') as data:
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2801854Z                 a = data['a']
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2802135Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2802458Z           The underlying file descriptor is closed when exiting the 'with'
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2802911Z           block.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2803149Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2803616Z         Examples
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2803879Z         --------
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2804155Z         Store data to disk, and load it again:
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2804510Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2804796Z         >>> np.save('/tmp/123', np.array([[1, 2, 3], [4, 5, 6]]))
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2805228Z         >>> np.load('/tmp/123.npy')
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2805549Z         array([[1, 2, 3],
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2805819Z                [4, 5, 6]])
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2806083Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2806357Z         Store compressed data to disk, and load it again:
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2806741Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2806968Z         >>> a=np.array([[1, 2, 3], [4, 5, 6]])
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2807308Z         >>> b=np.array([1, 2])
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2807616Z         >>> np.savez('/tmp/123.npz', a=a, b=b)
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2807977Z         >>> data = np.load('/tmp/123.npz')
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2808310Z         >>> data['a']
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2808571Z         array([[1, 2, 3],
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2808849Z                [4, 5, 6]])
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2809135Z         >>> data['b']
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2809395Z         array([1, 2])
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2809641Z         >>> data.close()
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2809902Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2810206Z         Mem-map the stored array, and then access the second row
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2810624Z         directly from disk:
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2810918Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2811182Z         >>> X = np.load('/tmp/123.npy', mmap_mode='r')
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2811550Z         >>> X[1, :]
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2812020Z         memmap([4, 5, 6])
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2812301Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2812517Z         """
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2812806Z         if encoding not in ('ASCII', 'latin1', 'bytes'):
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2813291Z             # The 'encoding' value for pickle also affects what encoding
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2813820Z             # the serialized binary data of NumPy arrays is loaded
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2814338Z             # in. Pickle does not pass on the encoding information to
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2814862Z             # NumPy. The unpickling code in numpy._core.multiarray is
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2815393Z             # written to assume that unicode data appearing where binary
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2815952Z             # should be is in 'latin1'. 'bytes' is also safe, as is 'ASCII'.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2816405Z             #
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2816736Z             # Other encoding values can corrupt binary data, and we
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2817288Z             # purposefully disallow them. For the same reason, the errors=
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2817893Z             # argument is not exposed, as values other than 'strict'
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2818375Z             # result can similarly silently corrupt numerical data.
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2818935Z             raise ValueError("encoding must be 'ASCII', 'latin1', or 'bytes'")
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2819404Z     
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2819752Z         pickle_kwargs = dict(encoding=encoding, fix_imports=fix_imports)
2025-01-24T13:52:24.2820193Z

2025-01-24T13:52:24.2822026Z             else:
